  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_5dad1785-87e9-490f-9c5d-4cd58b3515cd'
      });

  <span id="freeText8585377586901388854" style="display:none">Amber, the one real world, wherein all others, including our own Earth, are but Shadows. Amber burns in Corwin's blood. Exiled on Shadow Earth for centuries, the prince is about to return to Amber to make a mad and desperate rush upon the throne. From Arden to the blood-slippery Stairway into the Sea, the air is electrified with the powers of Eric, Random, Bleys, Caine, and all the princes of Amber whom Corwin must overcome. Yet, his savage path is blocked and guarded by eerie structures beyond imagining; impossible realities forged by demonic assassins and staggering horrors to challenge the might of Corwin's superhuman fury.' to 'Awakening in an Earth hospital unable to remember who he is or where he came from, Corwin is amazed to learn that he is one of the sons of Oberon, King of Amber, and is the rightful successor to the crown in a parallel world.</span>

          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {
            if ($('edition_1118509').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});

<div id="review_109169712" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/109169712" />
    <a title="Michael" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1036930-michael"><img alt="Michael" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1583425448p2/1036930.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/109169712?book_show_action=true">Jun 28, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michael" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michael" href="/user/show/1036930-michael">Michael</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Unknown Binding 9780839824275" href="/book/show/62014.Nine_Princes_in_Amber">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1036930-michael?shelf=1970s">1970s</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1036930-michael?shelf=most-popular-reviews">most-popular-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1036930-michael?shelf=fiction-that-speculates">fiction-that-speculates</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer109169712" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5885763466764388867">Roger,<br/><br/>No, it would be no problem at all! I'd be happy to respond to the first draft of your new fantasy novel. <br/><br/>Lets start with the good: I enjoyed your method of immersing the reader in your fantasy world. The protagonist's case of amnesia makes it so he must learn all the same things the reader needs to know. Protagonist Corwin regains his memory gradually, creating a sense of mystery throughout the first hundred pages that is quite entertaining. <br/><br/>Then. . . well, you lost me. I mean, it's so eso</span>
  <span id="freeText5885763466764388867" style="display:none">Roger,<br /><br />No, it would be no problem at all! I'd be happy to respond to the first draft of your new fantasy novel. <br /><br />Lets start with the good: I enjoyed your method of immersing the reader in your fantasy world. The protagonist's case of amnesia makes it so he must learn all the same things the reader needs to know. Protagonist Corwin regains his memory gradually, creating a sense of mystery throughout the first hundred pages that is quite entertaining. <br /><br />Then. . . well, you lost me. I mean, it's so esoteric. SHADOW REALMS, one for every combination of things that could be. Nine princes who can travel at will between these Shadow Realms. But there's really only ONE REAL WORLD, the world of Amber, of which all the other worlds are shadows. All of these princes want to be the king of Amber, and they struggle against each other for the throne . . .<br /><br />Well, one issue I have is that I'm not sure why I should side with Corwin. I'm not entirely convinced he's the "good guy." It's sort of like voting for Zeus instead of Hera. They're all egomaniacal wackjobs. <br /><br />And then you tell us, most of the way through the novel, each one of these brothers could technically make their own perfect reproduction of the original world of Amber, and ALL be kings of identical territories, AND COMPLETELY BYPASS ALL OF THIS FIGHTING TO THE DEATH?! So WHY. The FUCK. Should your reader care? As Tim Gunn would say, "This part has me worried." <br /><br />Before attempting to get this published, I HIGHLY recommend reconsidering how omnipotent this set-up will make your protagonist. At the very least, don't point out to your reader how ludicrous this whole war is. <br /><br />Another big issue I had was with your voice in this novel. I mean, sometimes you're all "If thou will help me to smote down ye evyl brother Eric, your noble brother Corwin shall be beholden to you." Then, a scene later, you're all, "I snuck out of the prison because I'm just that good. Dig? Solid." Are we casual? Are we not casual? Let's just decide. Either could work, but both don't. <br /><br />Also, you should know my interest tapered off drastically at the exact moment when things should've started getting exciting. The actual battle over Amber seemed . . . well, dull. First off, it's narrated kind of like an eight-year-old would narrate an action figure battle: "seven of the big furry red guys were killed. Three of their soldiers died. Seventy of the goodguys got blown off the snowy mountain. I stabbed some guy in the neck." You start a hell of a lot of sentences with "I did this." I was distracted by this. I could not visualize much of anything. I was tempted to skim.<br /><br />I'm sure this is your rough draft, despite the artificially yellowed pages and cool imitation 70's cover, mostly because of the excessive typos. My personal favorite: "the doors of good food." Did you mean Odors? I think so. I would fix that, and also doublecheck your punctuation. Commas seem like an unpredictable force in this book, happening sporadically and without logic. So, as I tell all my writing students, allways proofread. By the way, I loved the ironic quip on the front about "Hugo and Nebula Winning." After a few more drafts, that may become a reality, but remember my mantra: revise, revise, revise!<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5885763466764388867" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2363171033" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2363171033" />
    <a title="Evgeny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9340136-evgeny"><img alt="Evgeny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1544797852p2/9340136.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2363171033?book_show_action=true">Apr 17, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Evgeny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Evgeny" href="/user/show/9340136-evgeny">Evgeny</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9340136-evgeny?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2363171033" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15823945980629990129">I will make it brief. This series is the first of the two reasons 75% of the books I read are fantasy. Howard's Conan was the second reason. Thus the rating for this book and all following is 5 stars, period. <br/><br/>Do you really want the longer version? Even if you do not here it is. An unnamed guy woke up from drugged stupor in a hospital. His mental abilities were good enough to realize he was kept under drugs. He escaped and managed to acquire the address of a woman who placed him there - supposedl</span>
  <span id="freeText15823945980629990129" style="display:none">I will make it brief. This series is the first of the two reasons 75% of the books I read are fantasy. Howard's Conan was the second reason. Thus the rating for this book and all following is 5 stars, period. <br><br>Do you really want the longer version? Even if you do not here it is. An unnamed guy woke up from drugged stupor in a hospital. His mental abilities were good enough to realize he was kept under drugs. He escaped and managed to acquire the address of a woman who placed him there - supposedly his sister. The sister bit was true by the way, but I am getting ahead of myself. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1415614680i/11818925._SX540_.jpg" alt="Amber Princes" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Trying to regain his memory the poor guy soon learned the true story is much deeper than he suspected and to get to the bottom of this he needed to visit a mysterious and fascinating place called Amber. The only problem was, the place and all the roads leading to it were full of people literally dreaming of killing unlucky amnesiac. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1524014116i/25394090._SX540_.jpg" alt="True Amber" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>What follows is the best world-building in fantasy. I am very serious when I say nothing comes even remotely close. I tried to summarize it in my notes and realized that their length was not much shorter than the book itself (less than 150 pages). The latter also contained non-stop action and occasional descriptions that made the places in question come alive. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1524013799i/25394079._SY540_.jpg" alt="Amber" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This ability - to write short and to the point - is completely lost in modern literature. Modern writers think endless descriptions of food, heraldic, and so on constitute world-building. In case any aspiring fantasy writer read this let me assure you: these above constitute boredom. If you bored the book feels longer, so I can only assume this is done on purpose. This quote was written in Victorian Britain and still rings true:<br><pre><br>“Nothing is easier to write than scenery; nothing more difficult <br>and unnecessary to read.” <br><b>Jerome K. Jerome, Three Men on the Bummel</b><br></pre><br><br>Roger Zelazny knew how to write an exciting book that makes your imagination to go full throttle in minimal number of pages. Only true Masters possessed this ability. It feels almost like blasphemy to make long talks about such short and brilliant book, so I will shut up. Besides, I said everything I wanted about it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15823945980629990129" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_237186721" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/237186721" />
    <a title="Shannon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6773727-shannon"><img alt="Shannon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1579036502p2/6773727.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/237186721?book_show_action=true">Nov 18, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shannon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shannon" href="/user/show/6773727-shannon">Shannon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback " href="/book/show/9724168-nine-princes-in-amber">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6773727-shannon?shelf=fantasy-scifi">fantasy-scifi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6773727-shannon?shelf=action">action</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6773727-shannon?shelf=my-very-best-reads">my-very-best-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6773727-shannon?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6773727-shannon?shelf=books-reviewed">books-reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer237186721" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16887670789768961655">Man, all the good stuff has been said to let me be brief:<br/><br/>OVERALL FEELING: One of my favorite fantasy pieces; sort of starts out as a PI man who lost his memory and has to figure out that he's the prince of another world.<br/><br/><b> CONCEPT: What if Gods who looked like people created this world and all the other worlds through their Godly thoughts? And what if their father disappeared and there was a fight for the throne which shook all the worlds? And what if this Godly war led to doorways being opened wh</b></span>
  <span id="freeText16887670789768961655" style="display:none">Man, all the good stuff has been said to let me be brief:<br><br>OVERALL FEELING: One of my favorite fantasy pieces; sort of starts out as a PI man who lost his memory and has to figure out that he's the prince of another world.<br><br><b> CONCEPT: What if Gods who looked like people created this world and all the other worlds through their Godly thoughts? And what if their father disappeared and there was a fight for the throne which shook all the worlds? And what if this Godly war led to doorways being opened which should not have opened which could kill off these Gods? </b><br><br>MARKETING APPEAL: The Amber series is greatly loved; I imagine that it sold well; it took a first person point of view of a wise cracking PI type fantasy hero who discovered the realm of Amber; a conflict of sibling gods who are out for dominance and then discover a great evil. Superbly written.<br><br><span>[image error]</span><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380363415i/714759._SY540_.jpg" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>FAVORITE METAPHORS: “The night was bargaining weakly with the sun. The rising sun cast billions of bright shards into the foaming swell of the waters, and our eyes were dazzled by their dance so that we could not see beneath the surface.”<br><br>“The devil danced in his blue eyes . . . “<br><br> “I saw the fleet, sailing on a great ocean the color of blood. FAVORITE ACTION PASSAGE: As soon as we came to a halt, I flung open my door and leaped out --- barefooted yet! ... it!”<br><br>“ We pushed on, slowly, and there was blood on every step for as far back as I could see. There's a moral there, somewhere.” </i><br><br><i>FAVORITE DESCRIPTIVE PASSAGE: “It was about eight o'clock when the cab deposited me on a random corner in the nearest town. I paid off the driver and walked for around twenty minutes. Then I stopped in a diner, found a booth and had juice, a couple of eggs, toast, bacon and three cups of coffee. The bacon was too greasy.”<br><br>“Very, very much would they pay. An anger, a terrible one, flared within the middle of my body.”<br><br>“Answers? None.” </i><br><br><span>[image error]</span><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380363415i/714760._SX540_.jpg" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>DIALOGUE: I really liked the dialogue. It was terse and to the point with witty remarks all over the place, as well as some deep insights. Does a good job of not telling too much in the dialogue. No one is an idiot or constant talker. All, are sort of street smart. Corwin also has this fatalist attitude that I like. At times, he wonders as to the words he uses which makes it feel only more so that you are involved in the discussion with him (even if you can't talk back and ask questions). Good threats, too.<br><br><i> "Blood!" I called out. "Give me blood and vengeance this day, my warriors, and you will be remembered in Amber forever!" And as a man, they raised their weapons and cried out, "Blood!" And gallons --- no, rivers --- of it were let that day. We destroyed two more of Caine's raiders, replenishing our numbers from those of the survivors of our own fleet. As we headed toward a sixth, I climbed the mainmast and tried to take a quick count.<br><br>"Catch them, you fool!" And he did. </i><br><br>All I have to say is that Zelazny is my my favorite fantasy writer next to only one other writer: George Martin who is known for his incredible A SONG OF ICE AND FIRE series. This is surely one of the best series in fantasy even though it was written in the 1970s.<br><br>Note that the book directly after this one is Zelazny's “The Guns of Avalon”. A three part graphic novel was created from this tale in the 1990s and talks of a movie have been in the work for, well, decades.<br><br><b>CHARACTERS/DIALOGUE: A minus to A; STORY/PLOTTING: A minus to A; FRESHNESS (for its time): A to A plus; SETTING/TONE: B plus to A minus; NARRATIVE FIRST PERSON FLOW: A minus; OVERALL GRADE: A minus to A; WHEN LAST READ: 2001 (read three times) (revised review early April 2012). </b></span>
  <a data-text-id="16887670789768961655" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/25912578-nine-princes-in-amber">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2317475132" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12547925165139751759">⚔ <b>Zelazny <s>Freaks</s> Regulars</b> buddy read with my fellow <s>Freaks</s> Regulars <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2363171033' rel='nofollow noopener'>Evgeny</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2360163257' rel='nofollow noopener'>Choko</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/774613198' rel='nofollow noopener'>Eilonwy</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2351186456' rel='nofollow noopener'>Elena</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/183038569' rel='nofollow noopener'>Lee Who Just Came Back from the Dead</a> ⚔<br/><br/><b><u>Pre-review rating</u>: 3.33567458 stars</b>. <br/><b><u>Post-review rating</u>: 3 stars</b>. <i>Because I'm barbarous like that.</i><br/><br/><b>Okay</b>, let's get something out of the way real quick: yes, this is everyone and their barnacle's <b>mostest favoritest fantasy series ever</b>, and the one that, in most cases, <b>introduced them to the genre</b>, and the one that inspired <b>countless fantasy writers</b>. It also ha</span>
  <span id="freeText12547925165139751759" style="display:none">⚔ <b>Zelazny <s>Freaks</s> Regulars</b> buddy read with my fellow <s>Freaks</s> Regulars <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2363171033" rel="nofollow noopener">Evgeny</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2360163257" rel="nofollow noopener">Choko</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/774613198" rel="nofollow noopener">Eilonwy</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2351186456" rel="nofollow noopener">Elena</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/183038569" rel="nofollow noopener">Lee Who Just Came Back from the Dead</a> ⚔<br><br><b><u>Pre-review rating</u>: 3.33567458 stars</b>. <br><b><u>Post-review rating</u>: 3 stars</b>. <i>Because I'm barbarous like that.</i><br><br><b>Okay</b>, let's get something out of the way real quick: yes, this is everyone and their barnacle's <b>mostest favoritest fantasy series ever</b>, and the one that, in most cases, <b>introduced them to the genre</b>, and the one that inspired <b>countless fantasy writers</b>. It also happens to be the one <b>I obviously very read wrong</b>.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1484585617ra/21731736.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>Yeah yeah yeah, I know, this is quite outrageous and stuff. Hey, you might want to be careful with that finger of yours, you're going to end up spraining it if you don't stop wiggling it around like that. </i><br><br><b>Now</b> please do try and refrain from playing <b>Friendly Neighbourhood Troll</b> (FNT™), and lecturing me on <b>allllllllllllllllllll</b> the glorious things I <b>obviously missed</b> while reading this book. Why? Because <b>1</b>/I'm in a most <b>nefarious</b> mood today, so you might want to take a step back before I unleash the crustaceans and stuff, <b>2</b>/Sorry I <b>slightly forgot</b> what #2 was and <b>3</b>/I already KNOW that this delightful tale is packed with <b>dazzingly marvellous stuff</b>. How do I know, you ask? Sigh. With all due respect <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1490601881i/22325754.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, you really ask the silliest questions sometimes, my Flimsy Decapods. Because I bloody shrimping <b>READ IT</b>, that's why! *softly screams "DUH" at the top of her super sexey branchiae*<br><br><b>The truth is</b>, I haven't entirely lost it yet (don't worry, it won't last) and do realize that there is some <b>supremely good stuff</b> here. Ergo, I presently find my little self in quite the <b>predicament</b>. I mean, this book is mostly <b>brilliantly brilliant</b> indeed. Zelazny managed to build a <b>deliciously rich, complex world</b> in 150 miserable little pages. When it takes <s>most</s> <b>some authors</b> (who shall remain unnamed because I can't be ALL malevolent ALL the time please excuse the digression and stuff) 100+ books (and a half) in a series <s>not</s> to do the same, um, you know, <b>thing</b>. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1524155936ra/25402869.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>I know, right? And just you wait, for there's more captivating stuff on the way! I'm not <s>nearly</s> done yet! Be glad and rejoice!</i><br><br><b>So the world building</b> is pretty <b>luscious</b> and the story is original and fun and <b>intriguing</b> and the plot is <b>fast-paced</b> and there are <b>deviously deceitful characters</b> with potentially great potential and yes I am aware I already said most of this down there ↓↓ but who the fish cares anyway and there is lots of <b>Yummy Swashbuckling Type Stuff</b> (YSTS™) and I am most pleased that some of my <b>subaquatic cousins</b> are featured in the story and there are heavenly <b>Kentucky Fried Lizard Parts</b>, too and also <b>bid red guys + little hairy ones</b> and commas are <b>overrated</b> anyway.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1524156624i/25402894.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>This "but" here</b> ⤴ might seem quite innocently <b>inconspicuous</b> to you, and yet it is most completely responsible for the distressing (if a little Zelaznian) predicament I mentioned earlier. Because you see, my Flaky Arthropods, notwithstanding the <b>Stupendously Stupendous Stuff</b> (SSS™) this book is packed with, some stuff is <b>indeed rotten</b> in the state of Amber *cheerfully waves at her good chum Will S.*:<br><br>① <b>Anyone</b> who has read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/61998.Doorways_in_the_Sand" title="Doorways in the Sand by Roger Zelazny" rel="nofollow noopener">Doorways in the Sand</a> or <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/939645.Roadmarks" title="Roadmarks by Roger Zelazny" rel="nofollow noopener">Roadmarks</a> will tell you that Zelazny loves nothing better than to keep his <s>victims</s> readers' little grey cells <b>on their toes</b> and stuff (because yes, little grey cells have toes). So I obviously expected some serious <s>head</s> <b>exoskeleton scratching</b> to happen here, and this most delectable assumption was confirmed in the first chapters in the book. But then it all went <b>poof</b> and all was <b>revoltingly crystal clear</b> and despicably <b>simple</b> and my pincers were therefore left with nothing to <b>scratch</b> and got all itchy as a result and that is never good for <b>puny humans</b> in the immediate vicinity of my humble shrimpy abode but I slightly digress. Long paragraph tiny: too <b>straightforward</b> this story was, when most splendidly <b>befuddling</b> I expected it to be. <b>Quite disappointed this sad state of affairs left me</b>. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1484221606ra/21695289.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>Yes, some people manage to express their emotions in the most restrained way *and* be super stylish at the same time.</i><br><br>② The return of the <b>Ironing Boards of Doom</b> (IBoD™). Yes, I am afraid this is the awful truth indeed, as the characters in this book seem to have been infected by the much-feared <b>Flat as a Herd of Ironing Boards Virus</b> (FaaHoIBV™). Which is a teensy little bit slightly infuriating since they were all <b>so promising initially</b>. But <b>depth</b> they utterly lack and <b>emotions</b> they are unable to express and <b>act like lifeless machines</b> most of the time they do. So <b>give a fish</b> about them I never really came to. Which sucks big time. Especially since there's some <b>potential harem material</b> here *waves at prospective boyfriend Corwin* Now if that's not <b>overwhelmingly depressing</b>, I don't know what is.<br><br>③ Was this book written by <b>Zelazny's evil twin</b>, I wonder? The writing is shockingly <b>uneven</b> and <b>unbalanced</b> throughout the book. You get <b>loooooonnnng passages</b> about <s>not necessarily fascinating</s> stuff, and then <b>less than a ridiculous paragraph</b> about a battle: "we met. We fought. I won." Okay then. Then there are the <b>dialogues</b>. One minute the characters <b>are all</b>, <i>"I fear to fetch us steeds." "And I, also"</i> and the next they <b>are all</b>, <i>"Hey man, I don't dig this. Hey man, I don't dig that. Guys this, guys that, here a guy, there a guy, everywhere a guy…"</i> which kinda sorta <b>makes me go all</b>…<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1524162908i/25403264._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br> <b>Get the gist</b> of my predicament now? You don't? Oh, well. <br><br>➽ And the moral of this <b>Please Someone Tell Me Where I Can Take How To Write Concise Reviews 101 Classes This Is Getting Hopelessly Hopeless and Tiresomely Tiresome Crappy Non Review</b> (PSTMWICTHtWCR101CTIGHHaTTCNR™) is: have no fear, Zelaznian <s>Freaks</s> Enthusiasts, for I shall most promptly read book 2 and see the <b>glorious Zelaznian light</b> in all its splendour, after which we shall all live shrimpily ever after and stuff. <b>Then again maybe not</b>.<br><br>✎ <b>Book 2</b>: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2364353484" rel="nofollow noopener">Guns of Avalon</a> - <i>currently reading</i>.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1479540926i/21203689._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>[<b>Pre-review nonsense</b>]<br><br><b><u>Actual rating</u>: 3.33567458 stars</b>. <i>A most pathetic rating indeed. Bad, bad Sarah.</i><br><br>I should have rated this book <b>4 gloriously glittering stars</b>. Why? Because I say so, that's why. And <b>also maybe perhaps</b> because this book is <b>fun and entertaining</b> and features <b>Cool Devious Cunning Treacherous Characters</b> (CDCTC™) galore (+ also possibly <b>harem material</b>) and it's <b>action-packed</b>, too and the <b>world</b> is pretty fishing original, too and the <b>body count</b> is off the charts, too and <b>hahaha</b>, too and <b>stuff</b>, too. <br><br><b>Okay</b>, given how great this book sounds when I describe it, it seems pretty obvious I <b>read it wrong</b>. Then again maybe I read it right, but <b>rated it wrong</b>? Or did I actually read it wrong but <b>rated it right</b>? Hmmm...I think this demands <b>further investigation</b>. Please excuse me while I <b>energetically scrutinize</b> the unfathomable depths of my exoskeleton in search for an answer to this <b>most puzzling enigma</b>.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1516199112ra/24887998.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>Yes, this is what I look like when I'm in Full Energetically Scrutinizing Mode (FESM™). Pretty hot, huh?</i><br><br>➽ Full <b>I'm Doing the Preemptive Kidnapping Poof Gone Harem Thing on Corwin Because You Never Know and Stuff Crappy Non Review</b> (IMtPKPGHToCBYNKaSCNR™) to come.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_1025379682" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1025379682" />
    <a title="Markus" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26681101-markus"><img alt="Markus" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1421952301p2/26681101.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1025379682?book_show_action=true">Aug 13, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Markus" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Markus" href="/user/show/26681101-markus">Markus</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26681101-markus?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26681101-markus?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1025379682" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13314294212152071137"><i>All roads lead to Amber.</i>.<br/><br/>Nine brothers fight for the inheritance left behind by the disappearance of their father. The ultimate prize is the throne of Amber, the one real world, of which all other worlds are mere shadows and reflections.<br/><br/><i>Nine Princes of the Amber</i> is an interesting fantasy introduction with an intriguing concept. I really enjoyed reading the early parts, where the prince Corwin wakes up in a hospital on Earth with no memory of his past. I expected a more traditional fantasy when p</span>
  <span id="freeText13314294212152071137" style="display:none"><i>All roads lead to Amber.</i>.<br /><br />Nine brothers fight for the inheritance left behind by the disappearance of their father. The ultimate prize is the throne of Amber, the one real world, of which all other worlds are mere shadows and reflections.<br /><br /><i>Nine Princes of the Amber</i> is an interesting fantasy introduction with an intriguing concept. I really enjoyed reading the early parts, where the prince Corwin wakes up in a hospital on Earth with no memory of his past. I expected a more traditional fantasy when picking up this book, but instead got a story of Corwin and his companions travelling between worlds and attempting to reach Amber while also struggling to regain his memory and understanding of what’s going on.<br /><br />This combination of science fiction and fantasy was pretty interesting, and made even more so by the fact that the protagonist himself, as a result of his amnesia, holds as little information as the reader to begin with about the world of Amber and how it works. Thus the reader is able to follow Corwin’s journey and learn with him.<br /><br />Unfortunately, Zelazny’s writing is not very good, at least not at this early stage. It seems to blend many different styles of writing, which often ruins the atmosphere of the story and the setting, and also contains a number of mistakes throughout the book. Additionally the simplicity of the plot and the shallowness of characterisation made the quality suffer slightly. However, these are all negatives that can be easily corrected in sequels, and I’m ready to give dear Roger the benefit of doubt because of how intriguing the concept is.<br /><br />Overall, this is a very short and enjoyable introduction to one of the great fantasy series of the previous century.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13314294212152071137" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2360163257" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2360163257" />
    <a title="Choko" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27962805-choko"><img alt="Choko" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1475642755p2/27962805.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2360163257?book_show_action=true">Apr 17, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Choko" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Choko" href="/user/show/27962805-choko">Choko</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2360163257" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16925160420205246096"><b>*** 4 ***</b><br/><br/><b>
  <i>"...“I like libraries. It makes me feel comfortable and secure to have walls of words, beautiful and wise, all around me. I always feel better when I can see that there is something to hold back the shadows.” ..."</i>
</b><br/><br/>Nine Princes in Amber is the first installment in a series of 10 rather shortish books. They are divided into 2 arcs and the first one is told from Corwin’s perspective, while the next set make his son's story the main event. Although we see the happenings from this family </span>
  <span id="freeText16925160420205246096" style="display:none"><b>*** 4 ***</b><br /><br /><b>
  <i>"...“I like libraries. It makes me feel comfortable and secure to have walls of words, beautiful and wise, all around me. I always feel better when I can see that there is something to hold back the shadows.” ..."</i>
</b><br /><br />Nine Princes in Amber is the first installment in a series of 10 rather shortish books. They are divided into 2 arcs and the first one is told from Corwin’s perspective, while the next set make his son's story the main event. Although we see the happenings from this family line's POV, the real center of both arcs is the internal struggle of the family to deal with their inherited familial need to dominate the others of their bloodline by any means possible - betrayal, treachery, backstabbing, all breaks of honor and what we consider human empathy in all circumstances, all in the battle to capture and keep their birthright, the Crown of Amber, once belonging to their father, Oberon, who is currently and has been for a very long time missing, presumed dead. Whoever ends up with the crown will have to dodge the treachery of all his siblings and their allies, while ruling Amber and trying to protect its people from problems starting to emerge from the Shadows and the forces of Chaos.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>"...“there is Shadow and there is Substance, and this is the root of all things. Of Substance, there is only Amber, the real city, upon the real Earth, which contains everything. Of Shadow, there is an infinitude of things. Every possibility exists somewhere as a Shadow of the real.” ..."</i>
</b><br /><br />In this volume we are introduced to Corwin, who awakens in a hospital after an apparent car "accident", heavily drugged and kept this way on purpose, with severe amnesia and no idea of who he is, where he is, and only with an insistent sense of danger and the knowledge he needs to get out of there. In the beginning of the book he has to figure out who he is, find a way to go some place safe, discover who his enemies are, get some allies, play an obviously dangerous game by bluffing his way through it, and once he finds out not only who he is but also what he is, he has to make some martial decisions which would have sweeping consequences for many, many people... But most of all, he has to confront his brother Eric and take the Crown. Turns out, because of Eric and his mental influence, Corwin has been stuck on Earth for centuries, having a real-life first hand knowledge of things like the plague, the reign of Queen Elizabeth, Napoleon, the life in concentration camps, and all the wars in between. As he starts to remember, he discovers that he is one of the nine princes of Amber, the only World which is Real and True, while all other worlds, including our Earth, are just shadows thrown by it. It is the only "substance" while all the rest are "Shadows"... The opposite and opposing entity to Amber is Chaos. And Chaos is starting an offensive on the g-d-like siblings of Amber. Are they going to get to a point where they will put their in-fighting to the side in order to protect the World? <br /><br /><b>
  <i>"...“I walked among Shadows, and found a race of furry creatures, dark and clawed and fanged, reasonably manlike, and about as intelligent as a freshman in the high school of your choice-sorry, kids, but what I mean is they were loyal, devoted, honest, and too easily screwed by bastards like me and my brother. I felt like the dee-jay of your choice.” ..."</i>
</b><br /><br />Yep, those Amber G-ds sure are assholes!!! <br /><br />The siblings are all gifted with what to us is like super-powers, for them just part of their heritage. In most of the Shadow Worlds they are looked upon and worshiped as a pantheon of g-ds. The ones of The Blood are capable of traveling between the worlds by manipulating matter, adding and subtracting in a formula meant to solve for the destination they desire. I find this system absolutely fascinating and love the heck out of it. It is different, it is imaginative and very original, having in mind that the first book was created in the late 60's and published as a complete work in '71. It is a kind of a hybrid between Science Fiction and Fantasy and as every first work is not perfect, but it sure is entertaining. He does have all the female siblings as a second thought and females are not very present in the story, but I hope we get there eventually. What I love about this author the most is his ability to write in a minimalistic manner and short format, while packing every page with world-building and action. I have said before, he knows exactly the limits to keep us interested and never get bored!!! I can't wait to return and see what happens with the familial MMA cage match that is The Princes of Amber!!! <br /><br /><b>
  <i>"...“What an enormous chutzpah you possess," I told him. "What makes you better than the rest of us, and more fit to rule?" "The fact that I was able to occupy the throne," he replied. "Try and take it.” ..."</i>
</b><br /><br /><br />Now I wish you All Happy Reading and may you always find what you Need in the pages of a Good Book! <br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16925160420205246096" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText7732046045157828810" style="display:none">See my review under the one volume (omnibus) set...one of my favorite series. This is another classic that ought to be called a classic!<br /><br />Update:<br /><br />I read this one first...back when. It was in the 1970s. I have since grown a bit, aged quite a bit and...possibly even matured a little. I still love these books. I have also discovered audio books (this too happened some years ago and has been detailed elsewhere. My wife became very ill and was bed fast a long time, she also came to the point where she really couldn't read, so I began tracking down audio books for her. First I got books on cassette and later on CD. Since I had the books anyway I listened to them in my work vehicle).<br /><br />Since that time I have found I really like audio books and have often bemoaned that these books, the <i>Amber Series</i> were never done in audio.<br /><br />Well now it has been and as soon as Audible offered the books I began downloading them. <div id="review_632460412" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/632460412" />
    <a title="Pietro" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11506475-pietro"><img alt="Pietro" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1358362191p2/11506475.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/632460412?book_show_action=true">Jun 04, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Pietro" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Pietro" href="/user/show/11506475-pietro">Pietro</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11506475-pietro?shelf=chronicles-of-amber">chronicles-of-amber</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer632460412" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11378903114369681478">What a weird, weird book.<br/><br/>Nine princes in Amber begins with the protagonist, Corwin, waking up in an hospital room, with no memories of himself or his past. <br/>Soon after that he realizes he's been drugged for days and flees the building, meanwhile collecting bits of informations about his former life.<br/>Within a few chapters he learns he's one of the nine living princes of Amber, the only true world (of which every other world is but a Shadow. Literally.) and that this makes him basically a god.<br/>These </span>
  <span id="freeText11378903114369681478" style="display:none">What a weird, weird book.<br /><br />Nine princes in Amber begins with the protagonist, Corwin, waking up in an hospital room, with no memories of himself or his past. <br />Soon after that he realizes he's been drugged for days and flees the building, meanwhile collecting bits of informations about his former life.<br />Within a few chapters he learns he's one of the nine living princes of Amber, the only true world (of which every other world is but a Shadow. Literally.) and that this makes him basically a god.<br />These princes can, in fact, modify Shadow worlds with just a minor effort of will(but not Amber itself), travel freely between universes and do a number of other nifty things.<br />The rest of the book covers, more or less, his struggles to regain his memories and win the throne of Amber itself, now held by Eric, one of his brothers.<br /><br /><br />Too bad that, while having a great premise and being full of good ideas, the book fails (quite badly) to deliver.<br />Its first and most obvious fault is that it's so very hasty: Corwin goes from "I wake up without knowing who I am" to "I single-handedly wage war to decide the fate of all the universes" in about 30 pages! <br />It never takes time to build pathos or put some meat on the characters, and the result is that after a flying start the narration falls flat.<br />The whole second half of the book is made almost entirely of battles resolved in one-line sentences.<br />Just imagine a few dozen pages full of something like "We went there to fight A. Three hundred died. Then we fought B. Then C came and we fled. Then we fought C and a two thousand died."<br /><br /><br />Another big point is that this book does a lousy job of explaining things. Don't get me wrong I love books where you have to figure out things yourself, but here there's just a lot of random stuff thrown at you that you're supposed to take as a given.<br />Why are the princes so powerful? <br />What allows them to change reality? <br />Why can they change some things and not others? <br />Why on Earth do they all want Amber's throne? (since they could create an infinite number of worlds perfectly identical to it by simply wishing it) <br />Why doesn't gunpowder burn in Amber? (while matches work perfectly instead) <br /><br />The list could go on and on and on. At times you are given pathetic explanations on the lines of "Princes of Amber can change reality because they can". Why thank you very much, Mr. Zelazny.<br /><br />Plot resolutions are often plain ridiculous and lack any logic. <br />At some point in the book there's a battle on this loooong and narrow staircase climbing a mountain. These stairs are so narrow that only the two soldiers on the front can fight, and everyone else (we're talking a few thousands on each side) just stands there watching.<br />No one takes a bow, nor throws a fucking rock for that matter.<br />I'd write more about such plot holes but I don't want to make spoilers and I think I made my point already anyway. <br /><br />Last but not least, the language is a mix of archaic English and 70s slang. If ever there were any doubts that the two are not meant to go together, Nine princes in Amber wiped them away.<br />Apart from being very VERY annoying, this quaint (for want of a better and non offensive word) linguistc mix makes absolutely no sense.<br />Just think about it: our Earth is but one of an infinite number of Shadow world of which most characters (which, remember, are immortal gods) barely suspect the existence.. why the hell would they use American Idioms?? <br />A couple times is mentioned how they are actually speaking Amber's language.. and I must say I'm really, really curious as to how does "I dig thy stuff, brother" translate in Amberian(can't remeber the actual name).<br />The language is not the only part pervaded with random elements of American culture; the princes, for example,just can't help smoking about 20 packs of (branded) cigarettes per page. Where do they get them? No idea.<br /><br />I was constantly reminded of an uber-cheesy sci-fi movie from the 70s.<br />It's not an entirely terrible book and it holds some very cool concepts, but I hardly find it deserving all the praise it gets.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11378903114369681478" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1777651078" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1777651078" />
    <a title="Ivana Books Are Magic" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/56173179-ivana-books-are-magic"><img alt="Ivana Books Are Magic" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1578249636p2/56173179.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1777651078?book_show_action=true">Oct 06, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ivana Books Are Magic" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ivana Books Are Magic" href="/user/show/56173179-ivana-books-are-magic">Ivana Books Are Magic</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1777651078" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4679851699613961134">I remember, like it was yesterday, the moment I picked up this book in a library. Only it wasn't yesterday, it was about 15 years ago, but what is time when you're in love. I did fall in love with this series. Having read this book for the first time all that time ago, my initial reaction was a very favourable one. I thought this novel was absolutely mind-blowing. My thoughts today? They’re pretty much the same, in all honesty I can say that my original impression never really changed. If anythi</span>
  <span id="freeText4679851699613961134" style="display:none">I remember, like it was yesterday, the moment I picked up this book in a library. Only it wasn't yesterday, it was about 15 years ago, but what is time when you're in love. I did fall in love with this series. Having read this book for the first time all that time ago, my initial reaction was a very favourable one. I thought this novel was absolutely mind-blowing. My thoughts today? They’re pretty much the same, in all honesty I can say that my original impression never really changed. If anything, I’ve grown to love this novel even more. While I was reading Nine Princes in Amber for the first time, I felt like something life-changing has just happened to me. Perhaps I was not mistaken. I remember telling everyone at some high-school part how cool this book is. They all seemed to agree with me as far as the coldness of the whole concept of shadowy words goes. I’m not sure did I actually get anyone to read it, but it is never too late, right? That is why almost two decades later, I’m writing this review. This is still one of my favourite fantasy series of all time.<br /><br /><br />I love the genre mixing in this one, the way this novel opens as (an attempted) murder mystery and all of the sudden takes a turn towards fantasy is ingenious. Our protagonist Carl (who will later on discover his real name is Corwin) wakes us in a hospital, having no recollection of himself. His amnesia lasts for quite some time, making the events in the novel more mysterious and interesting. We’re in there with him, struggling to make sense of things, trying to unravel the complexities of his situation. Corwin escapes the hospital without much ado and having found the address of his sister, gets to her home shortly. Corwin may have lost his memory but not his style. He relies on his instincts to get as much information out of his nervous sister Flora as he can. Corwin at the start of The Nine Princes in Amber reminds me on heroes of noir novel, he seems like a tough and resourceful kind of guy that, like a cat, always lands on his fit and lives to fight another day. However, very early in the story Corwin gets his rug pulled under his feet and all it takes is one word: Amber.<br /><br /><br />I swear I could feel the hairs on my hands standing while I was reading about his initial reaction to this word and the funny thing is that in that this early in the story he (and we as readers) is totally clueless about what this word means, but as the mere mentioning of this word caused a storm in his head, he feels it must be an answer to all the questions he yet has to learn how to form. All roads lead into Amber. We won’t learn what that means for a while. Yet, I could sense it must be something big. His strong reaction suggested as much and Corwin is depicted as someone whose instincts are right one. He intuitively knows that he is not to trust his siblings and that they might in fact be trying to kill him. Wasn’t it a clever plot device to have a protagonist who is unaware of the fantasy elements in the story itself? The realization of the complexity of his world is something that he comes in terms with step at a time and in this way, we as readers, are saved from reading long explanations and descriptions. We’re showed, rather than told- and some say this is indicative of good writing. While they might not always be the case, I dare say it is in this novel.<br /><br /><br /> Anyhow, soon after Corwin’s ‘not so warm’ heart to heart talk with Flora, another character steps in the game. Random, his younger brother, true to his name, arrives out of the blue and brings trouble with him. The mystery of Amber is about to be told, but I won’t speak about how it will happen, because I want to avoid spoilers. If you’re thinking of reading this book, don’t go on and read some synopsis that reveals the plot. Where is the fun in that? I know there is a good change you’ve heard about it before. Even greater is the chance that having looked up the novel, you have had already came across the information, but just in case you didn’t- don’t read it. All you need to know is that you’re in for a ride. The Nine Princes In Amber starts up as a crime novel, but it ends up being an amazing fantasy one with an awe-inspiring cast of characters. So, who are the nine princes in Amber? I won’t tell you that. Are they well portrayed? They sure are. Are they about to do fantastic things? Yes, they will. There you go, it’s all you need to know as readers. Instead of giving up too much information, let’s just get back to talking about why and how this novel rocks. <br /><br /><br />First of all, I thought the premise of the book was absolutely brillant. If I’m not mistaken, at that particular point in time (seventies), parallel universes weren’t really the thing. Sure, the parallel universes aren’t something that is/was unheard of in fantasy, but the way this novel explored it was (and it still IS) something quite original. I’m not sure that even today I can think of a novel that has managed to achieve something that feels this credible, this well plotted and constructed. There is something almost psychological about the way it explains parallel universities and often in my life (I did say it was life-changing and you see I didn’t lie), I’ve wondered how much are we the creators of our own reality, how much of what we see is just our projection and just how much of the world gets changed with our projection. Roger deserves to be praised for the power of his imagination. The idea behind this series is really something and the way it gets developed is truly wonderful, but I’m getting ahead of myself.<br /><br /><br />The second thing that I really love about this novel is protagonist, Corwin. His character development in this one is perfect. It is not by any means drastic (that is reserved for the sequels), in fact, it is so subtle you can almost miss it. The way amnesia affected Corwin’s personality is fascinating. In a way he preserved his personality even when he lost his memory (and old soul one might say) and that was certainly showed in a convincing manner, yet this amnesia made him question not just everyone else but also first and foremost himself. The way he acts is the way he always acted but there is a worm of a doubt. Corwin is starting to question himself. What will come of it? If you’re anything like me, by the time you finish this novel, you will surely be very eager to learn. I don’t think I have ever had a crush on a literary character, but this one really got under my skin. He is still in there somewhere.<br /><br /><br />Thirdly, the apple doesn’t fall far from the tree. If Corwin is a great character (and he is masterfully developed and portrayed), then trust that his family might be a subject of interest. On other words, leave it to his family to make the things a lot more interesting. This is a highly dysfunctional and Machiavellian family, but what a joy to read about them. Court and dagger sort of thing but done in Roger’s style! Every sibling was as fascinating as the next one and among much cruelty, there is also sincere respect. They are who they are. Who they are isn’t always pretty- most of the time, it is kind of disturbing. There are no classical good guys in this one, not even the protagonist himself- but if you’re me, you’ll see him in a good light.<br /><br /><br />Finally, there is the language- pure poetry. This novel is absolutely lyrical. The way that lyricism clashes with Machiavellian politics creates quite an interesting contrast. The story is told from Corwin’s point of view, so he as characters, thanks to his creator, sounds deviously charming and painfully eloquent pretty much all of the time. Not that I think of it, it must be why he is so darn loveable, even when he is…. Well, read a see how that one might end. The style of writing is absolutely perfect for this novel because it gives it both its dreamy quality and its credibility (considering who Corwing is). Roger wrote this one beautifully and the sequels are not any different.<br /><br /><br />That's basically it, my favourite things about this novel are: the setting (the very idea and premise of this story), Corwin (such an amazing character), Corwin’s family (basically all the important characters in the novel) and the beautiful writing. Yes, that sums it up nicely! I’m not sure why it took me more than 1500 words to say that. ;) I guess I was feeling like elaborating a bit on it.<br /><br /><br />You know, I’m seriously thinking of writing a review for every book of this series. Why not? I did enjoy the whole series a great deal, so I might as well write about it. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4679851699613961134" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1662066072" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1662066072" />
    <a title="Graeme Rodaughan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/56397934-graeme-rodaughan"><img alt="Graeme Rodaughan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1464911366p2/56397934.jpg" /></a>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1662066072?book_show_action=true">Jun 07, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Graeme Rodaughan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Graeme Rodaughan" href="/user/show/56397934-graeme-rodaughan">Graeme Rodaughan</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Anyone who admires tremendous imagination</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56397934-graeme-rodaughan?shelf=contemporary-fantasy-fiction">contemporary-fantasy-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56397934-graeme-rodaughan?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56397934-graeme-rodaughan?shelf=dark-fantasy-book-series">dark-fantasy-book-series</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1662066072" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5366109859223628758"><b>Tolkien, Feist, Erikson - and Zelazny - all masters of epic fantasy, possessed of towering imaginations allied with the authorial skills to honor their visions.</b><br/><br/>Just finished what I estimate to be my 6th re-read of this book. It's still fresh, still gripping, still enthralling. I never tire of this tale of Corwin, prince of Amber. Lost to amnesia, thrown back into a multiverse of plotting princes and princesses who if not actively stabbing each other in the back will pause to gossip about the sta</span>
  <span id="freeText5366109859223628758" style="display:none"><b>Tolkien, Feist, Erikson - and Zelazny - all masters of epic fantasy, possessed of towering imaginations allied with the authorial skills to honor their visions.</b><br /><br />Just finished what I estimate to be my 6th re-read of this book. It's still fresh, still gripping, still enthralling. I never tire of this tale of Corwin, prince of Amber. Lost to amnesia, thrown back into a multiverse of plotting princes and princesses who if not actively stabbing each other in the back will pause to gossip about the state of play while drinking a fine whiskey and enjoying a good cigarette.<br /><br />The only problem is, while Corwin has been lost on Earth for about four hundred years without his memory he's picked up a few vices his siblings lack - compassion, a sense of honor, and a penchant for duty...<br /><br />Just noting that some readers have remarked that if a number of princely types were to be contesting for the empty throne of Amber, and were also blessed with the capability of finding shadow realms that looked just like Amber where they could rule forever - why didn't they - after all it would be so much easier.<br /><br />Let me introduce you to the distinction between the real and the unreal. The Real world is 'Amber,' the shadows are just that - pale reflections of the real world - i.e. not the real world.<br /><br />The <i>value</i> of ruling in the real world is qualitatively different from the value of ruling in a shadow world. Not the same, like chalk and cheese.<br /><br />For any of the contenders for the throne of Amber, this distinction is an acute one that pervades their world view.<br /><br />Imagine if you will, you are an immortal, and you have the option of choosing between real sex and masturbation for the rest of your immortal life.<br /><br />Which do you choose?<br /><br />And now you understand why the princes fight to win the throne of the one real Amber, and forsake the fake illusions of the shadow worlds they could easily rule.<br /><br />Recommended as a classic of epic fantasy.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5366109859223628758" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1993160516" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1993160516" />
    <a title="Darwin8u" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2294090-darwin8u"><img alt="Darwin8u" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1547440402p2/2294090.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1993160516?book_show_action=true">May 06, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Darwin8u" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Darwin8u" href="/user/show/2294090-darwin8u">Darwin8u</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2294090-darwin8u?shelf=2017">2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1993160516" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11259979279629755973"><i>"If danger was the price of memory and risk the cost of opportunity, then so be it. I'd stay."</i><br/>- Roger Zelazny, Nine Princes in Amber<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1494268428i/22699514._SY540_.jpg' width='400' height='480' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Let me throw my biases out in front. I am not a fan of fantasy. I have a sister-in-law who reads a lot of fantasy and has shelves and shelves of elves and elves and I mock her almost to tears about it. I view a lot of the genre filled with derivative crap. But, I have found a couple gems. I loved Tolkien's <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/33.The_Lord_of_the_Rings__The_Lord_of_the_Rings___1_3_' title='The Lord of the Rings (The Lord of the Rings, #1-3) by J.R.R. Tolkien' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Lord of the Rings</a>, White's <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/43545.The_Once_and_Future_King__The_Once_and_Future_King__1_4_' title='The Once and Future King (The Once and Future King #1-4) by T.H. White' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Once and Future King</a>, and</span>
  <span id="freeText11259979279629755973" style="display:none"><i>"If danger was the price of memory and risk the cost of opportunity, then so be it. I'd stay."</i><br>- Roger Zelazny, Nine Princes in Amber<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1494268428i/22699514._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="480" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Let me throw my biases out in front. I am not a fan of fantasy. I have a sister-in-law who reads a lot of fantasy and has shelves and shelves of elves and elves and I mock her almost to tears about it. I view a lot of the genre filled with derivative crap. But, I have found a couple gems. I loved Tolkien's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/33.The_Lord_of_the_Rings__The_Lord_of_the_Rings___1_3_" title="The Lord of the Rings (The Lord of the Rings, #1-3) by J.R.R. Tolkien" rel="nofollow noopener">The Lord of the Rings</a>, White's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/43545.The_Once_and_Future_King__The_Once_and_Future_King__1_4_" title="The Once and Future King (The Once and Future King #1-4) by T.H. White" rel="nofollow noopener">The Once and Future King</a>, and Wolfe's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/968868.The_Book_of_the_New_Sun__The_Book_of_the_New_Sun__1_4_" title="The Book of the New Sun (The Book of the New Sun #1-4) by Gene Wolfe" rel="nofollow noopener">The Book of the New Sun</a>. Anyway, I was asking a bunch of friends for their recommendations for BIG BOOKS and one of my friends recommended <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5367.The_Great_Book_of_Amber__The_Chronicles_of_Amber___1_10_" title="The Great Book of Amber (The Chronicles of Amber, #1-10) by Roger Zelazny" rel="nofollow noopener">The Great Book of Amber</a>. My first impulse was to say no, but he asked why not? I respect this friend and figured I'd at least give the Corwin books (the first five books of the Amber Chronicles) a shot this year. <br><br>So, Nine Princes. It was interesting. Not great, but Zelazny has an almost Hemingway/hard-boiled way with dialogue and prose. The structure of the book (amnesia of the main protagonist) was a novel way to introduce the series and allowed the world/universe to unfold gradually. These books are obviously creative genre pulp, and probably very good fantasy. I'm not sure yet, however, if I would say they are GREAT literature. But so far, I'm intrigued enough to read the next several. If for no other reason than it does what trash/pulp novels are supposed to do: entertain, without too deep or hard a commitment. Under that consideration, it was a success.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11259979279629755973" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_774613198" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/774613198" />
    <a title="Eilonwy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17237503-eilonwy"><img alt="Eilonwy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1506803497p2/17237503.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/774613198?book_show_action=true">Nov 26, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Eilonwy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Eilonwy" href="/user/show/17237503-eilonwy">Eilonwy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17237503-eilonwy?shelf=enjoyable-enough">enjoyable-enough</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17237503-eilonwy?shelf=frustrating">frustrating</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17237503-eilonwy?shelf=good-mythology">good-mythology</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17237503-eilonwy?shelf=occasional-moments-of-brilliance">occasional-moments-of-brilliance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer774613198" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3147379983933728719"><blockquote>A guy wakes up in a hospital, sure he doesn’t belong there but unable to remember anything about himself. A combination of luck and sharp thinking brings him back into contact with his family -- a group of backstabbing double-crossers all in competition for the throne of Amber, the only Real city in the universe. (Everywhere else, including Earth as we know it, is but Shadow.) Naturally our hero wants the crown for himself. But getting it is going to require real struggle, real sacrifice, and al</blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText3147379983933728719" style="display:none"><blockquote>A guy wakes up in a hospital, sure he doesn’t belong there but unable to remember anything about himself. A combination of luck and sharp thinking brings him back into contact with his family -- a group of backstabbing double-crossers all in competition for the throne of Amber, the only Real city in the universe. (Everywhere else, including Earth as we know it, is but Shadow.) Naturally our hero wants the crown for himself. But getting it is going to require real struggle, real sacrifice, and all-too-real pain. </blockquote>The first 50 pages of this book and the last 5 pages were absolutely brilliant 5-star storytelling. <br /><br />But everything in between? Sadly, not quite so much, for me, anyway. The rest of this book was a frustrating combination of vivid and inspired, but also dead boring. Too much time passes too quickly as Corwin, our hero, allies himself with various brothers, gathers armies from various Shadowlands, wages war on land and on sea, and eventually finds himself jailed. Years and years pass in a huge blur, during which time, as a reader, I connected with no one and felt no particular investment in the story. I couldn’t care less about Amber or even Rebma, its undersea companion nation where the story spends a little more time. <br /><br />But then those last few pages? Breathtakingly ingenious and pure Zelazny. <br /><br />So I’m in for at least the next volume, and trusting that maybe now it will get to a closer, more “real” story where I actually get to know and care about some of the characters, especially Corwin. <br /><br />Fingers crossed. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3147379983933728719" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
