<div id="review_113117645" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/113117645" />
    <a title="Ken" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/730754-ken"><img alt="Ken" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1565570004p2/730754.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/113117645?book_show_action=true">Jul 23, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ken" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ken" href="/user/show/730754-ken">Ken</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/730754-ken?shelf=finished-in-2010">finished-in-2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/730754-ken?shelf=classics-newly-read">classics-newly-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer113117645" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2350815999364474334">When I was a teenager (long ago in a country far, far away), I read Roger Zelazny's wonderful Amber series from start to finish in one huge gulp. Unfortunately, since then, the Amber books have only been in print as one big doorstop edition -- not the type of thing my 8th graders would pick up to read readily.<br/><br/>Imagine my eyes when my wife dragged me to an antique store here in Maine (OK, "junk" store) and I wandered into the used paperback books section and found 8 out of the 10 original paperbac</span>
  <span id="freeText2350815999364474334" style="display:none">When I was a teenager (long ago in a country far, far away), I read Roger Zelazny's wonderful Amber series from start to finish in one huge gulp. Unfortunately, since then, the Amber books have only been in print as one big doorstop edition -- not the type of thing my 8th graders would pick up to read readily.<br /><br />Imagine my eyes when my wife dragged me to an antique store here in Maine (OK, "junk" store) and I wandered into the used paperback books section and found 8 out of the 10 original paperbacks, all at $2 each. Whoa! I bought them ipso fasto and then went to Barnes &amp; Nobles on-line to find sellers who would have the remaining two. These cost me more due to the $3.99 shipping and handling (a.k.a. "highway and robbery"), but it was worth it to have the whole set in paperback form to add to my classroom library (where, no doubt, some of them will be lost or stolen this year... sob).<br /><br />Anyway, I decided to reread the first book in the series -- <i>Nine Princes in Amber</i> -- so I could book talk the entire series to my class this September. Amazingly, it held up over time. About the only 70s hangover (it was originally published in 1970) it suffers is the characters' constant lighting up of cigarettes and downing of drinks (wait, that still applies -- and it's not like cigarettes are going the way of the Edsel, either).<br /><br />I think it's a classic in its genre if only for the imagination that went behind the worlds Zelazny created (Amber, the Forest of Arden, Remba, etc.). I know the aficionados all say his <i>Lord of Light</i> is the classic, but that was more onerous to me. This one's a STORY. It's got plot. It's got nine brothers at each other's throats for the throne, each constantly changing alliances with the other for self-gain. And Corwin is just tough-guy fun to be around.<br /><br />I also love the concept of each prince (and princess -- as there are six of those as well) being a face card as a trump in decks carried by each of them. If you're in a tight spot and they are reachable, you can try to contact one by looking at the card. Sometimes the card will come to life and you can communicate, reaching a hand to it and thus being pulled to wherever that brother or sister happens to be.<br /><br />OK, so it appeals to the fantasy kid in me. Its medieval intrigues recast into the 20th century shows psychology as well as brute force at its Machiavellian best. The question is, will the 21st-century kids like it? I'll report back in the fall....</span>
  <a data-text-id="2350815999364474334" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2129146165" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2129146165" />
    <a title="Nandakishore Varma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6237864-nandakishore-varma"><img alt="Nandakishore Varma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1583648733p2/6237864.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2129146165?book_show_action=true">Sep 19, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nandakishore Varma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nandakishore Varma" href="/user/show/6237864-nandakishore-varma">Nandakishore Varma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780722194393" href="/book/show/1118509.Nine_Princes_in_Amber">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2129146165" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12025411716439409103">There must be some bad chemistry between Roger Zelazny and I. I read his award-winning novel <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13821.Lord_of_Light' title='Lord of Light by Roger Zelazny' rel='nofollow noopener'>Lord of Light</a> and was seriously underwhelmed. I explained why in my review, but still got pasted for bad-mouthing an American classic from an Indian viewpoint. Anyone interested in seeing the roasting I got can visit the comment thread on my review of that book.<br/><br/>I thought well, maybe I have been less than fair: this gentleman being one of the greats in the field of SF and fantasy, I should give him anothe</span>
  <span id="freeText12025411716439409103" style="display:none">There must be some bad chemistry between Roger Zelazny and I. I read his award-winning novel <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13821.Lord_of_Light" title="Lord of Light by Roger Zelazny" rel="nofollow noopener">Lord of Light</a> and was seriously underwhelmed. I explained why in my review, but still got pasted for bad-mouthing an American classic from an Indian viewpoint. Anyone interested in seeing the roasting I got can visit the comment thread on my review of that book.<br /><br />I thought well, maybe I have been less than fair: this gentleman being one of the greats in the field of SF and fantasy, I should give him another chance - and picked this book up from the library. No luck! I ended up being disappointed again, less so than before maybe because my expectations were lesser.<br /><br />The story as such is pretty simple. There are nine princely brothers who want to rule the kingdom of Amber (which is the only real realm, all others - including our earth - being shadows of it), and our first-person protagonist Corwyn is one of them. The problem is, currently power is held by Eric, another prince, who doesn't want to let go. So what happens when many people want a single seat of power happens in this novel too - war, murder and mayhem.<br /><br />The story starts abruptly with Corwyn trapped in our world without a memory. How he escapes from his confinement in a hospital and manages to reach Amber with the help of another brother Random is told entertainingly. The action moves at breakneck speed - to quote Stephen King, "the goofy speed of a silent film" - and is quite entertaining. However, once they reach Amber it becomes more of traditional fantasy fare, though still enjoyable.<br /><br />There are a lot of exciting fantasy devices - the Tarot pack which the princes use for communication; the Pattern where Corwyn regains his memory, in the undersea kingdom of Rebma, which is a mirror image of Amber; the fight on the endless stairs to the city - but it all felt too skeletal for me, like the outline for a novel. I am not a fan of large tomes, but in this case, I felt the novel would have benefited from a bit of fleshing out.<br /><br />Sorry, Mr. Zelazny, I think I am not the ideal reader for your novels.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12025411716439409103" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Stjepan Cobets" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44823204-stjepan-cobets"><img alt="Stjepan Cobets" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508476465p2/44823204.jpg" /></a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fan of Fantasy and SF</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44823204-stjepan-cobets?shelf=my-home-library">my-home-library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44823204-stjepan-cobets?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1778012869" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17692913843539383050">My rating 4.8<br/><br/>The book "Nine Princes in Amber (The Chronicles of Amber # 1)" by Roger Zelazny, is not without reason, classic science fiction and fantasy. The story and the world in which the action is happening is not easy to describe because there is as much shadow as Amber. Amber is the main and only city and all other shadows and even the Earth. Maybe ten years I have this book in my library, but I did not start reading, too many books, and too little time. But this is what I'm up to now and </span>
  <span id="freeText17692913843539383050" style="display:none">My rating 4.8<br /><br />The book "Nine Princes in Amber (The Chronicles of Amber # 1)" by Roger Zelazny, is not without reason, classic science fiction and fantasy. The story and the world in which the action is happening is not easy to describe because there is as much shadow as Amber. Amber is the main and only city and all other shadows and even the Earth. Maybe ten years I have this book in my library, but I did not start reading, too many books, and too little time. But this is what I'm up to now and I'm not sorry either because the book is great. I think a lot of things are written about this book, so I'm not going to write much about the content, but be assured that the book will be easy to put in a well-designed world and story. I would recommend the book to all lovers of science fiction and fantasy.</span>

<div id="review_164315749" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/164315749" />
    <a title="Kat  Hooper" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2177891-kat-hooper"><img alt="Kat  Hooper" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1533675060p2/2177891.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/164315749?book_show_action=true">Apr 28, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kat  Hooper" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kat  Hooper" href="/user/show/2177891-kat-hooper">Kat  Hooper</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2177891-kat-hooper?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer164315749" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1976642590737680723">Originally Posted at <a href='http://www.fantasyliterature.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>FanLit</a>.<br/><br/>“I’d get what I needed and take what I wanted and I’d remember those who helped me and step on the rest. For this, I knew, was the law by which our family lived, and I was a true son of my father.”<br/><br/>When Corwin wakes up in a private hospital after driving his car over a cliff, he has no idea who he is. When he realizes that he has healed too fast and that he’s being drugged so he’ll stay unconscious, he decides that he better find out what’s going on.<br/>The truth is strang</span>
  <span id="freeText1976642590737680723" style="display:none">Originally Posted at <a href="http://www.fantasyliterature.com" rel="nofollow noopener">FanLit</a>.<br /><br />“I’d get what I needed and take what I wanted and I’d remember those who helped me and step on the rest. For this, I knew, was the law by which our family lived, and I was a true son of my father.”<br /><br />When Corwin wakes up in a private hospital after driving his car over a cliff, he has no idea who he is. When he realizes that he has healed too fast and that he’s being drugged so he’ll stay unconscious, he decides that he better find out what’s going on.<br />The truth is strange: Corwin is one of the nine princes of Amber, the one true world, but for centuries he’s been exiled in the Shadowland we call Earth. The accident has actually dislodged the spell that his brother Eric was using to keep him out of Amber because Corwin is the biggest threat to Eric’s sovereignty there.<br /><br />Nine Princes in Amber is the first (rather short) installment in a long epic that describes, from Corwin’s perspective and later his son’s, the struggle of his family to deal with both their internal treacheries and the evil forces that assail them from the forces of Chaos. In Nine Princes in Amber, Corwin must figure out who he is, assess his resources, gather some allies, wonder whether his father is dead or alive, and make a move on the throne of Amber. Here we learn what Corwin has been doing for centuries on Earth, meet several of his siblings, discover the way in and out of Amber, meet a race of people who live under the sea, and discover some of the special powers of Corwin’s family.<br /><br />Ah… Corwin’s family… if you can call them a “family.” Corwin’s own description for them is “Machiavellian,” and that about covers it. Corwin and his brothers and sisters are clever, sophisticated, sarcastic, and extremely ambitious. They constantly scheme and plot to outmaneuver each other as they vie for political power. If you knew these people in real life, you’d probably hate them, but in Zelazny’s hands they’re kind of charming. These are people who plan to live forever, have the ability to design their own worlds to plunder, are incapable of trust, and have no reason to think about anyone other than themselves. In the end, Corwin rages against his brother and makes a rash decision that will negatively affect Amber’s future.<br /><br />THE CHRONICLES OF AMBER was highly imaginative when it was published in the 1970s and it remains fresh and original today. The magic system is creative, Zelazny’s writing style is solid, the story is fast-paced, exciting, and mature. Plot twists and cliffhangers make it hard to stop reading. You’ll definitely want to have The Guns of Avalon, the second book in the series, ready to go as soon as you finish Nine Princes in Amber.<br /><br />Nine Princes in Amber is a re-read for me because Audible Frontiers has recently produced THE CHRONICLES OF AMBER on audio — something I have been waiting years for. They’ve chosen one of their best narrators for Zelazny’s most famous work: Alessandro Juliani. He’s got the perfect voice and style to play Corwin, so I’m really pleased with this production. If you’re an audio reader, you’ll definitely want to download this classic!</span>
  <a data-text-id="1976642590737680723" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/216557302?book_show_action=true">Sep 28, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Logan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Logan" href="/user/show/3420149-logan">Logan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer216557302" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11191557151544783027">I hate, hate, HATED this book. I hate this series, but at least the other books are better than this horrendous beginning.<br/><br/>Nothing in this book makes any sense. The system of magic (if there is one) has no parameters or rules--one minute the prince can travel between worlds in a car that he can also change around at will, the next he can't do anything, the next he's walking through doors drawn in the walls, the next he's doing something else weird and nonsensical. <br/><br/>The only motive anyone has in th</span>
  <span id="freeText11191557151544783027" style="display:none">I hate, hate, HATED this book. I hate this series, but at least the other books are better than this horrendous beginning.<br /><br />Nothing in this book makes any sense. The system of magic (if there is one) has no parameters or rules--one minute the prince can travel between worlds in a car that he can also change around at will, the next he can't do anything, the next he's walking through doors drawn in the walls, the next he's doing something else weird and nonsensical. <br /><br />The only motive anyone has in this book is a loosely-defined desire for the throne of Amber, which is the only real world in existence. There are nine princes and, I think, some princesses, and some of them are dead, and one of them has the throne but the main character (another prince with highly selective amnesia) wants it. <br /><br />The dialogue in this book is patently ridiculous, but it improves in sequels. The characters seem to alternate between "old-ish" English (I can't really elaborate on this) and modern talk, even going so far as to incorporate slang. <br /><br />As I said before, magic in this book is vague. It is used as a deus ex machina several times (main character in trouble, new character shows up with special magic trick to bail him out, new character disappears forever) but with no consistency; one day the character(s) can alter the fabric of reality itself and the next day they can't do anything useful. There are no rules to the magic except when rules are convenient to move the plot.<br /><br />Again, the sequels improve on all of these, but not enough for me to enjoy this series, and especially this terrible, extremely highly overrated book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11191557151544783027" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1430295631" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1430295631" />
    <a title="Ryan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/35415186-ryan"><img alt="Ryan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1494401888p2/35415186.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1430295631?book_show_action=true">Jun 01, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ryan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ryan" href="/user/show/35415186-ryan">Ryan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1430295631" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5186378133707819728"><u>The Good</u>:<br/>Zelazny’s writing is brilliant. He makes it so easy to just fall into the story, no matter how bizarre the setting. The setting here is the ‘Amberverse’ (I’m sure there is a better or at least more official name for it) and our own universe is a very small part of it. The kind of magic at work in this setting is the type that allows immensely powerful people to warp reality with their thoughts, yet still allows them to have car accidents and get beaten up by a bunch of regular thugs. So</span>
  <span id="freeText5186378133707819728" style="display:none"><u>The Good</u>:<br />Zelazny’s writing is brilliant. He makes it so easy to just fall into the story, no matter how bizarre the setting. The setting here is the ‘Amberverse’ (I’m sure there is a better or at least more official name for it) and our own universe is a very small part of it. The kind of magic at work in this setting is the type that allows immensely powerful people to warp reality with their thoughts, yet still allows them to have car accidents and get beaten up by a bunch of regular thugs. Somehow it works. I loved the protagonist too.<br /><br /><u>The Bad</u>:<br />It isn’t confusing so much as very opaque. This is a fantasy story, with ubiquitous magic, so whether or not a problem can be solved with a snap of the fingers is obviously a matter of author fiat. This requires constant exposition to keep the reader in the loop. I found it interruptive. In the hands of a less skilled writer I think it would have been unbearable.<br /><br /><u>'Friends' character the protagonist is most like</u>:<br />Corwin is an everyday bloke who just happens to be heir to the shining pinnacle of reality. He is very much Chandler, though being immortal makes him a bit like Joey too.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5186378133707819728" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Jenny (Reading Envy) by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/2867426-scott-danielson">Scott Danielson</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68030-jenny-reading-envy?shelf=read2014">read2014</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer333272095" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13993461808752880571">Add this to the list of fantasy series and authors I had never read. I picked up a volume that includes this book and the next one, from a used book store in Georgetown, SC that has since burned down along with most of the downtown.<br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1413165787i/11474027._SX540_.jpg' width='400' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Luckily, I had rescued this book by purchasing it from the obscure science fiction and fantasy corner in the attic, along with a Catherynne Valente. It has a child's bookplate with a unicorn in the inside front cover, and this really made it feel like a living book!<br/><br/>Th</span>
  <span id="freeText13993461808752880571" style="display:none">Add this to the list of fantasy series and authors I had never read. I picked up a volume that includes this book and the next one, from a used book store in Georgetown, SC that has since burned down along with most of the downtown.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1413165787i/11474027._SX540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Luckily, I had rescued this book by purchasing it from the obscure science fiction and fantasy corner in the attic, along with a Catherynne Valente. It has a child's bookplate with a unicorn in the inside front cover, and this really made it feel like a living book!<br><br>The basic premise of the book is a man waking up in a hospital in New York with amnesia. He slowly learns his connection to the world of Amber. My favorite part absolutely had to be the journey into Remba, the underwater mirror world to Amber. <br><br>There are little slang words that slip in, like "dig" for "I get it" and "creamed" for defeated that place this book soundly in the 1970s. I'll definitely read the next one!</span>

<div id="review_40533366" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/40533366" />
    <a title="Manny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1713956-manny"><img alt="Manny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442491692p2/1713956.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/40533366?book_show_action=true">Dec 20, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Manny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Manny" href="/user/show/1713956-manny">Manny</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1713956-manny?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer40533366" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3562019219963162858">A couple of weeks ago, I posted a review of <i>Les Trois Mousquetaires</i>, where I argued that it was the spiritual father of the modern French trash novel. Since then, I've been having three parallel discussions with my wife, Jordan and notgettingenough about what it is that makes something into a trash novel. Three out of the four of us incline to the view that it's the quality of being mass-produced; a trash novel is one that has been hastily constructed according to an existing formula, with a min</span>
  <span id="freeText3562019219963162858" style="display:none">A couple of weeks ago, I posted a review of <i>Les Trois Mousquetaires</i>, where I argued that it was the spiritual father of the modern French trash novel. Since then, I've been having three parallel discussions with my wife, Jordan and notgettingenough about what it is that makes something into a trash novel. Three out of the four of us incline to the view that it's the quality of being mass-produced; a trash novel is one that has been hastily constructed according to an existing formula, with a minimum of independent thought. In practice, this means that most trash novels are genre fiction, since formulas typically belong to a specific genre. Notgettingenough, the outlier, is reluctant to accept that the label 'trash novel' has any meaning. She argues that some generally accepted masterpieces were produced quickly, and that an author of sufficient talent can turn out something in a few weeks which is better than a 'literary' novel that might have taken years to write. True, but I would say these cases are rare, and don't invalidate the basic argument. They mainly show that some people are far more gifted than others.<br /><br />But there are certainly books and authors that lurk uneasily in the no-mans-land around Trashville proper. Zelazny's <i>Amber</i> series comes to mind. This book, the first one, is IMHO a good, original fantasy/SF novel. It's exciting, quite well-written, and contains a bunch of ingenious ideas. (Those magic packs of cards! The fight on the Endless Stair!) But, as the series progressed, I thought it got more tired and stale with each book that appeared, and I would, alas, have to classify the last ones as formulaic trash. Zelazny was no longer creating, just recombining, and it became horribly like listening to a group of D&amp;D players discussing the week's happenings in their current game.<br /><br />I wonder what this example shows? Perhaps any novel, or indeed any work of art, turns into trash into if it's copied enough times, or copied with sufficient lack of skill. The funny thing is that it can happen even when the person doing the copying is the one who wrote the original template.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3562019219963162858" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Lee" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4162390-lee"><img alt="Lee" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1525386186p2/4162390.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/183038569?book_show_action=true">Jul 08, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lee" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lee" href="/user/show/4162390-lee">Lee</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4162390-lee?shelf=old-school-scifi">old-school-scifi</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer183038569" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10746353270999247750">Well. If a Bookshelf/tag was ever a perfect description, then 'oldschool scifi' is it.<br/><br/>A solid 3.5 stars, (I wonder why GR has refused to listen for all these years on half star ratings?)<br/><br/>This is the second read of this story for me. The first was over 25 years ago and was when I was just getting into fantasy. I kind of liked it, but rushed through it and never picked up book 2. To be honest, I can't actually remember finishing it, so it was probably a dnf. <br/><br/>My second read through, found me older, </span>
  <span id="freeText10746353270999247750" style="display:none">Well. If a Bookshelf/tag was ever a perfect description, then 'oldschool scifi' is it.<br /><br />A solid 3.5 stars, (I wonder why GR has refused to listen for all these years on half star ratings?)<br /><br />This is the second read of this story for me. The first was over 25 years ago and was when I was just getting into fantasy. I kind of liked it, but rushed through it and never picked up book 2. To be honest, I can't actually remember finishing it, so it was probably a dnf. <br /><br />My second read through, found me older, wiser, relaxed in my new reading chair with a glass of red wine and thankful that committing to my first group read in over a year was only a 117 pages long. A perfect way to get back into social reading and the crew I read with are very social :)<br /><br />Back to the book, since this is supposed to be a review. Zelazny's writing is quite unique, he manages to tell a story with considerably less words than anyone I know. Talk about not fleshing out the story with wordy sentences (looking at you China Meiville). He manages to pack into just over 100 pages a story with enough back story to not make you feel Malazanish, enough character build to clearly define the main characters, some drip feed magic to keep you guessing and a hint at a much bigger plot. Some scenes are very very short and that is different, I am used to big drawn out battles with descriptions of arm muscles being torn and wrenched till they pop etc. In amber it is more like 'he rode straight at me on his horse, sword aloft, I stepped inside his arm and pulled him off. I won'. Simple, effective and time to move on.<br /><br />You do really need to read with book 2, commit to 250 pages. I think a lot of people, the younger me included, probably feel there wasn't enough in the first book, but I am confident that after reading the fist 5 pages of book 2, that the story is going to unfold before us, in a deliciously old fashioned way. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10746353270999247750" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2928392077" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2928392077" />
    <a title="William" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/99853253-william"><img alt="William" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1602426860p2/99853253.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2928392077?book_show_action=true">May 20, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="William" class="user" itemprop="url" name="William" href="/user/show/99853253-william">William</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/99853253-william?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2928392077" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12676366792022253113">After a few days off to replace all my window blinds, I'm finally able to spend some time reading again. I listened to an audiobook narrated by Roger Zelazny himself, and it was a real treat. Not only was the book fantastic, but Roger has one of the best "bedtime stories" voices ever. His voice is not boring, so as to put one to sleep, but it's soothing, and as you can imagine he does his best to bring his work to life.<br/><br/>This type of fantasy writing is a real interest of mine. Prosaic and imaginat</span>
  <span id="freeText12676366792022253113" style="display:none">After a few days off to replace all my window blinds, I'm finally able to spend some time reading again. I listened to an audiobook narrated by Roger Zelazny himself, and it was a real treat. Not only was the book fantastic, but Roger has one of the best "bedtime stories" voices ever. His voice is not boring, so as to put one to sleep, but it's soothing, and as you can imagine he does his best to bring his work to life.<br /><br />This type of fantasy writing is a real interest of mine. Prosaic and imaginative, but at the same time serious and mature. This is a bloody tale of a merciless world where trust does not exist but at the same time, it's a story of comradery and kinship. Roger had a knack for rooting his fantasy in the real world and also throwing off the yoke of fantasy convention. Brevity is one thing that really shines in Zelazny's work, Nine Princes in Amber taking up the same amount of space as the average modern fantasy fight scene. Nine Princes in Amber felt crisp and fresh throughout, partly due to its brevity, and excellent pacing. Martha Wells is another author that I feel does this style very well, so it's no coincidence I love her books as well.<br /><br />In spite of its brevity, Nine Princes in Amber manages to convey an interesting, and original setting that I greatly enjoyed. Delivering a few meaningful details about the setting through dialog is far more effective than several chapters of descriptive narration, for my tastes anyway.<br /><br />I consider Nine Princes in Amber a true classic, and due to its age is a nice break from modern trends. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12676366792022253113" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2440451569" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2440451569" />
    <a title="Anthony" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4009947-anthony"><img alt="Anthony" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1534088626p2/4009947.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2440451569?book_show_action=true">Apr 19, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anthony" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anthony" href="/user/show/4009947-anthony">Anthony</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/25912578-nine-princes-in-amber">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4009947-anthony?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4009947-anthony?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4009947-anthony?shelf=sf-group-2018">sf-group-2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2440451569" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7115382982630749259">This was my second encounter with the work of the renowned SFWA Grand Master Roger Zelazny, and I was much less enchanted by it than I was by his winsome, enjoyably macabre A Night in the Lonesome October. I will say that this novel provides moments of a sort of tough-minded, ironic poetry, and it’s clear that he had a rich imagination, and a welcome willingness to experiment with style and anachronisms. I just never really cared all that much what would happen to the narrator, Corwin, or to his</span>
  <span id="freeText7115382982630749259" style="display:none">This was my second encounter with the work of the renowned SFWA Grand Master Roger Zelazny, and I was much less enchanted by it than I was by his winsome, enjoyably macabre A Night in the Lonesome October. I will say that this novel provides moments of a sort of tough-minded, ironic poetry, and it’s clear that he had a rich imagination, and a welcome willingness to experiment with style and anachronisms. I just never really cared all that much what would happen to the narrator, Corwin, or to his many brothers and sisters. <br /><br />I don’t know anything about Zelazny’s predilections, but I suspect that he was ingesting no small amount of hallucinogenic substances while he was writing this short but densely packed little novel. Some of the trippiness was somewhat mesmerizing, and some of it was dull, but it was always pretty trippy. <br /><br />I read this at this moment because it was mentioned in the wonderful Among Others, and it’s the first of a 5-book series, but I don’t think I’ll be reading on to discover what happens to Corwin and Amber, as much as I can admire aspects of Zelazny’s achievement here. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7115382982630749259" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=unique-magic">unique-magic</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer41553064" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12654588965773591654">4.o stars. Excellent novel that, despite its age, retains much of its originality and all of its fun. A pioneer among the novels involving the "multiverse," this story portrarys multiple dimensions (or multiuple realities) in fantasy rather than science fiction terms. <br/><br/>Corwin, an immortal and powerful (think god-like) prince of Amber awakes in a hospital with no memories of who he is or how he got there. He quickly escapes and comes to learn that he is heir to the throne of Amber (the one true wo</span>
  <span id="freeText12654588965773591654" style="display:none">4.o stars. Excellent novel that, despite its age, retains much of its originality and all of its fun. A pioneer among the novels involving the "multiverse," this story portrarys multiple dimensions (or multiuple realities) in fantasy rather than science fiction terms. <br /><br />Corwin, an immortal and powerful (think god-like) prince of Amber awakes in a hospital with no memories of who he is or how he got there. He quickly escapes and comes to learn that he is heir to the throne of Amber (the one true world when all of the other realities, including our Earth, are just shadows). Corwin's other brothers and sisters are engaged in an epic struggle accross shadow realms in an attempt to claim the throne of Amber for theselves. Only one can win. Recommended. <br /><br />Nominee: Mythopoeic Fantasy Award (1970). </span>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('UIMbLFFb7un+WK065M6xgA1QSclZRC76w0tSnYZzJj1DgauhVWAEC9BwRm9g9m4XEaH3U//vc0aKvk6KuvnxlQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('xMbeXvKB5pmyK8wXTpbtw9Re+UH1Da/dbHLN8PfPxirXxG7T9roMe5wDJ0LKrjJUyK9H21Om8mElh9Hny0URgg==')})
  }

Author Michael Moorcock, already a major player in science fiction, cemented his position in the fantasy pantheon with the five-book Elric saga, of which Elric of Melniboné is the first installment. The book\'s namesake, the brooding albino emperor of the dying nation of Melniboné, is a sort of Superman for Goths, truly an archetype of the genre.\n\nThe youthful Elric is a cynical and melancholy king, heir to a nation whose 100,000-year rule of the world ended less than 500 years hence. More interested in brooding contemplation than holding the throne, Elric is a reluctant ruler, but he also realizes that no other worthy successor exists and the survival of his once-powerful, decadent nation depends on him alone. Elric\'s nefarious, brutish cousin Yrkoon has no patience for his physically weak kinsman, and he plots constantly to seize Elric\'s throne, usually over his dead body. Elric of Melniboné follows Yrkoon\'s scheming, reaching its climax in a battle between Elric and Yrkoon with the demonic runeblades Stormbringer and Mournblade. In this battle, Elric gains control of the soul-stealing Stormbringer, an event that proves pivotal to the Elric saga. --Paul Hughes<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"5203558638702149210\" href=\"#\"       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/3619.Roger_Zelazny">About Roger Zelazny</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/3619.Roger_Zelazny"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1207671346p3/3619.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/3619.Roger_Zelazny">Roger Zelazny
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
3,062
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer5035719479938545389">Roger Zelazny made his name with a group of novellas which demonstrated just how intense an emotional charge could be generated by the stock imagery of sf; the most famous of these is <i>A Rose for Ecclesiastes</i> in which a poet struggles to convince dying and sterile Martians that life is worth continuing. Zelazny continued to write excellent short stories throughout his career. Most of his novels dea</span>
  <span id="freeText5035719479938545389" style="display:none">Roger Zelazny made his name with a group of novellas which demonstrated just how intense an emotional charge could be generated by the stock imagery of sf; the most famous of these is <i>A Rose for Ecclesiastes</i> in which a poet struggles to convince dying and sterile Martians that life is worth continuing. Zelazny continued to write excellent short stories throughout his career. Most of his novels deal, one way or another, with tricksters and mythology, often with rogues who become gods, like Sam in <i>Lord of Light</i>, who reinvents Buddhism as a vehicle for political subversion on a colony planet.<br /><br />The fantasy sequence <i>The Amber Chronicles</i>, which started with <i>Nine Princes in Amber</i>, deals with the ruling family of a Platonic realm at the metaphysical heart of things, who can slide, trickster-like through realities, and their wars with each other and the related ruling house of Chaos. Zelazny never entirely fulfilled his early promise—who could?—but he and his work were much loved, and a potent influence on such younger writers as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/346732.George_R__R__Martin" title="George R. R. Martin" rel="nofollow noopener">George R. R. Martin</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1221698.Neil_Gaiman" title="Neil Gaiman" rel="nofollow noopener">Neil Gaiman</a>.<br /><br />He won the Nebula award three times (out of 14 nominations) and the Hugo award six times (out of 14 nominations). His <a href="http://aok.lib.umbc.edu/specoll/Zelazny/index.php" rel="nofollow noopener">papers are housed</a> at the Albin O. Khun Library of the University of Maryland, Baltimore County (UMBC).<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roger_Zelazny">http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roger_Ze...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="5035719479938545389" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
